This was requested by former Episode IX director [Colin Trevorrow](/wiki/Colin_Trevorrow "Colin Trevorrow"),[[46]](#cite_note-46) who also asked Johnson to include the shot of Poe and Rey introducing themselves.[[47]](#cite_note-Trevorrow_Empire-47) [Carrie Fisher](/wiki/Carrie_Fisher "Carrie Fisher") worked with Johnson on some of the dialogue, in sessions that he described as "stream-of-consciousness ad-lib."[[45]](#cite_note-SWCO_2017:_10_Things_We_Learned-45) Per a suggestion from Fisher, several of the film's characters wear jewelry of some type.[[48]](#cite_note-48) Hamill was surprised by the changes in his character, and had to formulate a personal backstory for the character so as to play the character effectively.[[49]](#cite_note-49)[[50]](#cite_note-50) In an interview with [*Polygon*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polygon_(website) "wikipedia:Polygon (website)"), Hamill described the security measures on set: "You get your pages in the morning, and they take them from you as you walk so they can shred them before it somehow leaks. You have security lines you have to walk through, both to and from set. And, not to mention, you have to wear these big monk hoods to protect your costume from drones."[[51]](#cite_note-51) By June 2016, filming was "in the home stretch."[[52]](#cite_note-52) Principal photography wrapped on July 22, 2016.[[53]](#cite_note-53)

### Post-production[]

Johnson began editing on [August 15](/wiki/August_15 "August 15"), 2016.[[54]](#cite_note-54) His first cut ran over three hours, and included full sequences that were cut from the final film.[[55]](#cite_note-55) Carrie Fisher passed away on [December 27](/wiki/December_27 "December 27"), 2016. Though she had completed filming,[[56]](#cite_note-56)[[57]](#cite_note-57) she hadn't recorded all of her [ADR](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dubbing_(filmmaking)#ADR.2Fpost-sync "wikipedia:Dubbing (filmmaking)"). This required significant work by the film's sound editors.[[18]](#cite_note-14_Things-18) Relatively few [pick-ups](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking) "wikipedia:Pick-up (filmmaking)") were required, mostly dealing with the Canto Bight sequence and refining the Holdo character.[[58]](#cite_note-58) [John Williams](/wiki/John_Williams "John Williams") returned to compose the score, which was recorded from December 2016 to June 2017. He utilized a 101-piece orchestra and a 64-voice choir.[[59]](#cite_note-59) On [September 21](/wiki/September_21 "September 21"), 2017, Johnson revealed that post-production was complete.[[60]](#cite_note-60)

## Release and reception[]

Disney chairman Bob Iger originally announced the release date for Episode VIII of [May 26](/wiki/May_26 "May 26"), [2017](/wiki/2017 "2017"), forty years and one day after the release of *Star Wars*: Episode IV *A New Hope*,[[61]](#cite_note-Rogue_One_SW.com-61) though the release date was later pushed back to [December 15](/wiki/December_15 "December 15"), 2017.[[2]](#cite_note-Release_Date-2) Rian Johnson first publicly discussed the film in a panel at [Celebration Europe](/wiki/Celebration_Europe_(2016) "Celebration Europe (2016)").[[62]](#cite_note-SW-'Future_Filmmakers'_Come_Together_for_Special_Panel_at_Star_Wars_Celebration_Europe_2016-62) The film's title, *The Last Jedi*, was announced on [January 23](/wiki/January_23 "January 23"), 2017. The title announcement was accompanied with a release of a logo for the film featuring the *Star Wars* logo in red rather than its traditional yellow. This color change, previously seen with *Return of the Jedi* and with "[Brothers](/wiki/Brothers_(episode) "Brothers (episode)")" and "[Revenge](/wiki/Revenge_(episode) "Revenge (episode)")," installments of *[Star Wars: The Clone Wars](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars "Star Wars: The Clone Wars")* focused on [Darth Maul](/wiki/Maul "Maul"), led some to speculate that the film's creators may have been hinting at dark events within the film.[[63]](#cite_note-sithred-63) The title's announcement also launched a frenzy of online speculation in regard to the identity of the "last Jedi," with some noting that the term "Jedi" can be used plurally.[[64]](#cite_note-cnet-64) (Foreign translations also had the title as plural.[[65]](#cite_note-65)[[66]](#cite_note-66)[[67]](#cite_note-67)) However, Rian Johnson later said that it refers specifically to Luke Skywalker.[[68]](#cite_note-Rian_Johnson_Luke_Skywalker-68)

Footage of *The Last Jedi* was shared with Disney shareholders in March 2017, including a look at the beginning of the film, which happens immediately following the ending of *The Force Awakens*.[[69]](#cite_note-shareholders-69) Disney CEO Bob Iger, having seen the film, referred to it as a "perfect chapter" in the saga, stating, "I can promise you it's worth the wait."[[70]](#cite_note-perfectchapter-70) On [April 11](/wiki/April_11 "April 11"), Hamill and Ridley appeared on [*Good Morning America*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Good_Morning_America "wikipedia:Good Morning America") to promote the Force for Change charity;[[71]](#cite_note-71) one of the three rewards was a trip for two to the premiere of *The Last Jedi*.[[72]](#cite_note-SW-Be_a_Force_For_Change_for_the_Chance_to_Win_a_Trip_to_the_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Premiere_and_More-72) Cast and crew featured in a *Last Jedi* panel at [Celebration Orlando](/wiki/Celebration_Orlando "Celebration Orlando").[[73]](#cite_note-SW-Kathleen_Kennedy_and_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Director_Rian_Johnson_to_Appear_at_Star_Wars_Celebration-73) At the end of the panel, Johnson debuted a teaser poster and teaser trailer.[[74]](#cite_note-The_Last_Jedi_panel-74) The film was featured in the May 2017 issue of [*Vanity Fair*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine) "wikipedia:Vanity Fair (magazine)") (for which the cast and crew were photographed on-set by [Annie Leibovitz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Annie_Leibovitz "wikipedia:Annie Leibovitz")) and both the August and December 2017 issues of [*Entertainment Weekly*](/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly_Books "Entertainment Weekly Books").[[75]](#cite_note-75)[[76]](#cite_note-76)[[77]](#cite_note-77) Johnson and the cast again appeared at July's [D23](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/D23_(Disney) "wikipedia:D23 (Disney)"), during which a behind-the-scenes featurette was released.[[78]](#cite_note-SW-D23_2017:_New_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Behind-the-Scenes_Footage_Revealed_and_More-78) In the lead-up to release, cast and crew made various media appearances to promote the film, including [*Ellen*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Ellen_DeGeneres_Show "wikipedia:The Ellen DeGeneres Show"),[[79]](#cite_note-79) *Good Morning America*,[[80]](#cite_note-80)[[81]](#cite_note-81) [*Live with Kelly and Ryan*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Live_with_Kelly_and_Ryan "wikipedia:Live with Kelly and Ryan"), [*The Tonight Show*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon "wikipedia:The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon"), [*Jimmy Kimmel Live!*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jimmy_Kimmel_Live! "wikipedia:Jimmy Kimmel Live!"),[[82]](#cite_note-82) [*Conan*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Conan_(talk_show) "wikipedia:Conan (talk show)"),[[83]](#cite_note-83) and [*The Late Show With Stephen Colbert*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Late_Show_With_Stephen_Colbert "wikipedia:The Late Show With Stephen Colbert").[[84]](#cite_note-84) Cast members were also spotlighted in contemporary issues of [*Elle*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elle "wikipedia:Elle"),[[85]](#cite_note-85)[[86]](#cite_note-86) [*TIME*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_(magazine) "wikipedia:Time (magazine)"),[[87]](#cite_note-87) [*Esquire*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Esquire_(magazine) "wikipedia:Esquire (magazine)"),[[88]](#cite_note-88)[[89]](#cite_note-89) [*Rolling Stone*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rolling_Stone "wikipedia:Rolling Stone")[[90]](#cite_note-90) and [*The New York Times*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_New_York_Times "wikipedia:The New York Times"),[[91]](#cite_note-91) and Johnson and the cast participated in Facebook/Twitter Q&As.[[92]](#cite_note-92)[[93]](#cite_note-93)

The theatrical trailer and poster debuted on [October 9](/wiki/October_9 "October 9"), 2017 during [*Monday Night Football*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monday_Night_Football "wikipedia:Monday Night Football"), after which tickets went on sale.[[94]](#cite_note-94)[[95]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Theatrical_Poster_Revealed-95) Johnson advised spoiler-wary fans to avoid the trailer.[[96]](#cite_note-96) On [October 24](/wiki/October_24 "October 24"), [*USA Today*](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/USA_Today "wikipedia:USA Today") published an exclusive behind-the-scenes video.[[97]](#cite_note-97) A TV spot known as "Awake" debuted during the [November 1](/wiki/November_1 "November 1") broadcast of the [World Series](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_Series "wikipedia:World Series").[[98]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_TV_Spot_Features_New_Glimpses_of_Luke,_Rey,_and_More-98) Behind-the-scenes content was shown before theatrical screenings of other Disney movies.[[99]](#cite_note-99) The official *Star Wars* [Tumblr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tumblr "wikipedia:Tumblr") held a contest in which fan art was showcased at the film's world premiere,[[100]](#cite_note-100) which was held on [December 9](/wiki/December_9 "December 9"), 2017.[[101]](#cite_note-SW-Watch_the_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Red_Carpet_Live_at_StarWars.com-101)

## Continuity[]

The film shows Rey and Poe meeting for the first time. Their meeting was originally depicted in a scene cut from *Star Wars: The Force Awakens*, which appeared in the film's [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens_(novelization) "Star Wars: The Force Awakens (novelization)").[[102]](#cite_note-TwitterPabloContinuity-102)

In a discussion about Vice Admiral Holdo's tactic used to destroy the *Supremacy*, Lucasfilm Story Group member [Pablo Hidalgo](/wiki/Pablo_Hidalgo "Pablo Hidalgo") cited a similar maneuver that appeared in an episode of *Star Wars: The Clone Wars*, and that Holdo's maneuver was under unique circumstances[[103]](#cite_note-Pablo_Holdo_Tweet-103)—echoing a 2018 comment made by Johnson to [/Film](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki//Film "wikipedia:/Film"): "The fact that Hux doesn't see it coming means it's probably not a standard military maneuver. I think it was something that Holdo pulled out of her butt in the moment."[[104]](#cite_note-HoldoSlashfilm-104)

## Adaptations and tie-in media[]

The film's product line debuted on [September 1](/wiki/September_1 "September 1"), 2017, known as [Force Friday](/wiki/Force_Friday "Force Friday") II;[[105]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars_Force_Friday_II_Coming_September_1,_2017-105) [Target](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Target_Corporation "wikipedia:Target Corporation") launched its Force Friday campaign early with a video centered on Rey and female fans.[[106]](#cite_note-106) [Like with](/wiki/Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens "Journey to Star Wars: The Force Awakens") *The Force Awakens*,[[107]](#cite_note-Journey_to_TFA-107) the months leading up to the debut of *The Last Jedi* saw the release of several novels, short stories, comics, reference books, and activity books known collectively as [Journey to *Star Wars: The Last Jedi*](/wiki/Journey_to_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi "Journey to Star Wars: The Last Jedi"). The media, written and created by several different authors, cover various topics related to *The Last Jedi* as well as other aspects of the *Star Wars* universe.[[108]](#cite_note-Journey_to_TLJ-108) Toy merchandise includes many plush toys based on the porgs introduced in the film,[[109]](#cite_note-popsugar-109)[[110]](#cite_note-i4u-110) as well as various action figures, including action figures of porgs.[[111]](#cite_note-flickeringmyth-111)

Lucasfilm arranged licensing tie-ins with [Ample Hills](https://www.amplehills.com),[[112]](#cite_note-112) [Build-A-Bear Workshop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Build-A-Bear_Workshop "wikipedia:Build-A-Bear Workshop"),[[113]](#cite_note-113) [Cargo Cosmetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cargo_(cosmetics) "wikipedia:Cargo (cosmetics)"),[[114]](#cite_note-114) [Christian Louboutin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christian_Louboutin "wikipedia:Christian Louboutin"),[[115]](#cite_note-SW-Christian_Louboutin_on_the_Force-Powered_Fashion_of_His_Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Shoes-115) [Go-Gurt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go-Gurt "wikipedia:Go-Gurt"),[[116]](#cite_note-116), [Dole](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dole_Food_Company "wikipedia:Dole Food Company"),[[117]](#cite_note-117) [General Mills](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_Mills "wikipedia:General Mills"),[[118]](#cite_note-Six_Tie-Ins-118) [Hot Topic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_Topic "wikipedia:Hot Topic"),[[119]](#cite_note-119) [Nissan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nissan "wikipedia:Nissan"), [Philips](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philips "wikipedia:Philips"),[[118]](#cite_note-Six_Tie-Ins-118) [rag & bone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/rag_%26_bone "wikipedia:rag & bone"),[[120]](#cite_note-120) [Samsung](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samsung "wikipedia:Samsung"),[[121]](#cite_note-121) [Verizon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Verizon_Communications "wikipedia:Verizon Communications") and [Vizio](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vizio "wikipedia:Vizio").[[118]](#cite_note-Six_Tie-Ins-118) The UK's [Royal Mail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Royal_Mail "wikipedia:Royal Mail") released a series of *The Last Jedi*–themed postal stamps.[[122]](#cite_note-122) Disney added *The Last Jedi*–themed content to its *[Star Tours: The Adventures Continue](/wiki/Star_Tours:_The_Adventures_Continue "Star Tours: The Adventures Continue")* ride,[[123]](#cite_note-DPB-Star_Wars-themed_Land_at_Disney's_Hollywood_Studios_To_Dazzle_at_Night,_New_Star_Tours_Adventure_Coming-123) including the new planet Crait.[[124]](#cite_note-DPB-New_Star_Tours_Adventure_Revealed_at_Star_Wars_Celebration-124) The video game *[Star Wars Battlefront II](/wiki/Star_Wars_Battlefront_II "Star Wars Battlefront II")* features sequel-trilogy characters as they appear in *The Last Jedi*.[[125]](#cite_note-125) *[Star Wars: Galaxy of Heroes](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Galaxy_of_Heroes "Star Wars: Galaxy of Heroes")* introduced *The Last Jedi* characters and material.[[126]](#cite_note-EA-Content_Update_11/8/2017-126) [LEGO](/wiki/LEGO "LEGO") released an online minigame, "The Last Jedi" 360 Experience.[[127]](#cite_note-127) [ILMxLAB](/wiki/ILM_Immersive "ILM Immersive")'s *[Star Wars: Droid Repair Bay](/wiki/Star_Wars:_Droid_Repair_Bay "Star Wars: Droid Repair Bay")* is a virtual-reality experience that ties into the film.[[128]](#cite_note-SW-Become_a_Resistance_Mechanic_in_the_New_VR_Experience_Star_Wars:_Droid_Repair_Bay-128)

The film's [soundtrack](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_(soundtrack) "Star Wars: The Last Jedi (soundtrack)") was released in physical form and digital download on December 15, 2017, the same date as the film's theatrical premiere.[[129]](#cite_note-soundtrack-129) Many of the books previously announced on Force Friday were also released on this day; the rest, including the [novelization](/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi:_Expanded_Edition "Star Wars: The Last Jedi: Expanded Edition") and a number of other adaptations, were released in early [2018](/wiki/2018 "2018").

### Home video[]

The film was released on digital platforms on [March 13](/wiki/March_13 "March 13"), 2018 and on physical media on [March 27](/wiki/March_27 "March 27").[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130) Multiple physical editions were released:

* [Best Buy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Best_Buy "wikipedia:Best Buy") exclusive (Blu-ray/DVD/Digital; SteelBook packaging)[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130)
* Best Buy exclusive (4k/Blu-ray/Digital; SteelBook packaging)[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130)
* DVD only[[131]](#cite_note-Movie_Club-131)
* Multi-screen Edition (Blu-ray/Digital)[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130)
  + Disney Movie Club–exclusive Multi-screen Edition (includes DVD copy and lithograph)[[131]](#cite_note-Movie_Club-131)
* [Target](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Target_Corporation "wikipedia:Target Corporation") exclusive (Blu-ray/DVD/Digital; includes "Meet the Porgs" featurette and a 40-page booklet)[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130)
* Ultimate Collector's Edition (4K/Blu-ray/Digital)[[130]](#cite_note-Home-130)
* [Walmart](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Walmart "wikipedia:Walmart") exclusive (Blu-ray/DVD/Digital; interchangeable covers)[[132]](#cite_note-132)

Bonus features include:

* *The Director and the Jedi* – Go deep behind the scenes with writer-director Rian Johnson on an intimate and personal journey through the production of the movie—and experience what it's like to helm a global franchise and cultural phenomenon.
* *Balance of the Force* – Explore the mythology of the Force and why Rian Johnson chose to interpret its role in such a unique way.
* Scene Breakdowns
  + "Lighting the Spark: Creating the Space Battle" – Get a close-up look at the epic space battle, from the sounds that help propel the action, through the practical and visual effects, to the characters who bring it all to life.
  + "Snoke and Mirrors" – Motion capture and Star Wars collide as the filmmakers take us through the detailed process of creating the movie's malevolent master villain.
  + "Showdown on Crait" – Break down everything that went into creating the stunning world seen in the movie's final confrontation, including the interplay between real-word locations and visual effects, reimagining the walkers, designing the crystal foxes, and much more.
* *Andy Serkis Live! (One Night Only)* – Writer-director Rian Johnson presents two exclusive sequences from the movie featuring Andy Serkis' riveting, raw on-set performance before his digital makeover into Snoke.
* *Deleted Scenes* – With an introduction and optional commentary by writer-director Rian Johnson.
* *Audio Commentary* – View the movie with in-depth feature audio commentary by writer-director Rian Johnson.

Each purchase also grants access to a music-only version of the film.[[133]](#cite_note-133)

## Reception ‡[]

:   "*The ultimate intent was not to strip away—the intent was to get to the basic, fundamental power of myth. And ultimately I hope the film is an affirmation of the power of the myth of Star Wars in our lives.*"
:   ―Rian Johnson[[134]](#cite_note-Johnson_Empire_2022-134)

*Star Wars* creator George Lucas called the film "beautifully made."[[135]](#cite_note-135) Conversely, actor Mark Hamill voiced: "I'm sort of like a musician. I read the music, and I try to play it to the best of my ability. That doesn't necessarily mean I like the tune, but that's not my job."[[136]](#cite_note-Hamill-DenofGeek-136)

About negative reactions, Rian Johnson commented "Lucas never made a 'Star Wars' movie by sitting down and thinking, 'What do the fans want to see?' And I knew if I wrote wondering what the fans would want, as tempting as that is, it wouldn't work, because people would still be shouting at me, 'Fuck you, you ruined "Star Wars,' and I would make a bad movie. And ultimately, that's the one thing nobody wants."[[137]](#cite_note-137) In an interview conducted by *USA Today*, actress Daisy Ridley was asked if the backlash against Johnson came as a surprise to her. Ridley responded: "I wasn't surprised, no. It's just a different thing. Everyone's going to have an opinion now anyway on the Internet, but I also think it's fair. If people hold something incredibly dear and think they know how it should be and it's not like that, it's fair for people to think they were done wrong," adding, "It doesn't mean they were."[[138]](#cite_note-Ridley-USAToday-138)

As projected, the film took a domestic box office in its opening weekend of well over $200 million, a final figure of an estimated $220 million, and an overall global box office of approximately $450 million. It was predicted to break the billion-dollar barrier within days, as fans flocked to the box office for the Christmas holiday weekend.[[139]](#cite_note-rottenboxoffice-139) In 2018, the film received four [Academy Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academy_Awards "wikipedia:Academy Awards") nominations (including Original Score, Visual Effects, Sound Editing, and Sound Mixing),[[140]](#cite_note-SW-Star_Wars:_The_Last_Jedi_Receives_4_Oscar_Nominations-140) and won [AARP's](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AARP "wikipedia:AARP") "Best Movie for Grownups" Award.[[141]](#cite_note-141)

In late 2019, JJ Abrams, director of *The Force Awakens* and *The Rise of Skywalker*, told *Rolling Stone*: "When I read his first draft, it made me laugh, because I saw that was his take and his voice. I got to watch cuts of the movie as he was working on it, as an audience member. And I appreciated the choices he made as a filmmaker that would probably be very different from the choices that I would have made. Just as he would have made different choices if he had made Episode VII."[[142]](#cite_note-142) He also told *The New York Times*: "On the other hand, it's a bit of a meta approach to the story. I don't think that people go to 'Star Wars' to be told, 'This doesn't matter.'" Abrams added that the sequel trilogy was "a story that I think needed a pendulum swing in one direction in order to swing in the other."[[143]](#cite_note-143)
